They played a bilateral series in Harare at the start of this year with ZImbabwe taking the series 2-1. This series, however, will be an interesting one to follow. Ireland are part of the T20 World Cup 2024 that Zimbabwe missed out of. But their last T20I assignment was in August against India, where they showed the fight and yet lost. As for Pakistan, we can expect them to bounce back now that they have had some time in Ireland after an extended period of playing at home. However, the question remains whether they'll look to score quickly throughout the innings and not leave all the heavy lifting towards the end. The tourists will require a more disciplined bowling performance. Saim: "Pakistan has never been the same ever since the hammering by India in the Asia Cup. I look to that day as when the team's downfall began and they've never recovered." We can't underscore the importance of psychological factors in any competitive sport. Without grit and resilience, athletes tend to crumble under pressure, and maintaining a strong mindset is pivotal to success at this level. Pakistan didn't have the most memorable year, starting with the Asia Cup, followed by the ODI World Cup in India and a couple of bilateral series. But now it's time to start anew, leaving all the emotional baggage behind and focusing on the T20 World Cup. One aspect of the game that Babar could improve is his game assessment and tactics. After the first match, he mentioned they were 10 runs short of par and couldn't finish well. Instead of having a specific total in mind and a par score before the game, why not aim to post imposing totals and push your limits? GormintAunty: "First time in a long time I don't really feel that excitement before a Pak match. This last year has to be one of the worst in Pakistan cricketing history and that's saying something given our past. Although I hope its just the darkest before dawn bit and we take the WC by storm. <strong>2pm: </strong> Welcome to Ireland v Pakistan, the second T20I of the three-match series, and ESPNcricinfo's ball-by-ball coverage of the game. I hope it's a walloper of a contest. Pakistan will look to bounce back while Ireland will eye a historic series win. Let's see who's going to win the second tussle. I am Rvel Zahid and I'll bring you the action. I believe that the frequent changes in the PCB, coaching staff, and managerial roles over the past year or so have caused disturbance within the Pakistan cricket team. Perhaps the team is not as cohesive and united as it once was, and we mustn't overlook the importance of the game's mental aspects. The constant chopping and changing, the sudden axing of Shaheen Afridi after just one series against New Zealand has seemingly affected the team's environment Top athletes must develop a thick skin when competing at this level. Regardless of what has transpired with the captaincy changes and other distractions, the focus must shift to the upcoming World Cup. In the last game, <a href="https://www.espncricinfo.com/series/ireland-vs-pakistan-2024-1426828/ireland-vs-pakistan-1st-t20i-1426830/match-report">Andrew Balbirnie's bold onslaught</a> deflated Pakistan. It's becoming increasingly common for Pakistan to get deflated when facing a strong counter-attack, especially while defending scores. The same happened last month when Mark Chapman went berserk in the third T20I at the Rawalpindi Cricket Stadium. There have been issues with the batters' strike rate. Pakistan used to rely on a particular winning method: the opening pair of Mohammad Rizwan and Babar Azam would set a platform, albeit often at a lower strike rate, but the team would post middling totals, and then the bowling would usually bail them out of trouble. However, the bowling arsenal is not as potent and consistent as it used to be. The bowling lacked the kind of discipline that we saw in the 2022 World Cup. The percentage of full tosses, half-volleys, and missed wide yorkers was higher in the last game, which invariably released all the pressure. Shadab Khan, in his current form as a bowler, is not providing the stability that Pakistan expects from an experienced bowling all-rounder. Abrar Ahmed could be a much better wicket-taking option, and he is capable of bowling in the powerplay. What do you think?

They produced a stunning performance, especially with the bat, with Balbirnie leading the way. Harry Tector and George Dockrell put Pakistan under pressure with their pyrotechnics, and their approach towards chasing down the target was superb. Ireland's bowling attack will add further balance with the addition of Joshua Little, who will join the squad for the World Cup. They are shaping up well for the big event and have a history of springing surprises and pulling off major upsets. Expect more of the same from Ireland. As for Pakistan, we can expect them to bounce back now that they have had some time in Ireland after an extended period of playing at home. However, the question remains whether they'll look to score quickly throughout the innings and not leave all the heavy lifting towards the end. The tourists will require a more disciplined bowling performance. Mohammad Amir will be available for selection today, and his addition will certainly strengthen the pace attack, given his fair amount of experience playing in similar conditions. Saim: "Pakistan has never been the same ever since the hammering by India in the Asia Cup. I look to that day as when the team's downfall began and they've never recovered." We can't underscore the importance of psychological factors in any competitive sport. Without grit and resilience, athletes tend to crumble under pressure, and maintaining a strong mindset is pivotal to success at this level. Pakistan didn't have the most memorable year, starting with the Asia Cup, followed by the ODI World Cup in India and a couple of bilateral series. But now it's time to start anew, leaving all the emotional baggage behind and focusing on the T20 World Cup. One aspect of the game that Babar could improve is his game assessment and tactics. After the first match, he mentioned they were 10 runs short of par and couldn't finish well. Instead of having a specific total in mind and a par score before the game, why not aim to post imposing totals and push your limits? GormintAunty: "First time in a long time I don't really feel that excitement before a Pak match. This last year has to be one of the worst in Pakistan cricketing history and that's saying something given our past. Although I hope its just the darkest before dawn bit and we take the WC by storm. <strong>2pm: </strong> Welcome to Ireland v Pakistan, the second T20I of the three-match series, and ESPNcricinfo's ball-by-ball coverage of the game. I hope it's a walloper of a contest. Pakistan will look to bounce back while Ireland will eye a historic series win. Let's see who's going to win the second tussle. I am Rvel Zahid and I'll bring you the action. I believe that the frequent changes in the PCB, coaching staff, and managerial roles over the past year or so have caused disturbance within the Pakistan cricket team. Perhaps the team is not as cohesive and united as it once was, and we mustn't overlook the importance of the game's mental aspects. The constant chopping and changing, the sudden axing of Shaheen Afridi after just one series against New Zealand has seemingly affected the team's environment Top athletes must develop a thick skin when competing at this level. Regardless of what has transpired with the captaincy changes and other distractions, the focus must shift to the upcoming World Cup. In the last game, <a href="https://www.espncricinfo.com/series/ireland-vs-pakistan-2024-1426828/ireland-vs-pakistan-1st-t20i-1426830/match-report">Andrew Balbirnie's bold onslaught</a> deflated Pakistan. It's becoming increasingly common for Pakistan to get deflated when facing a strong counter-attack, especially while defending scores. The same happened last month when Mark Chapman went berserk in the third T20I at the Rawalpindi Cricket Stadium. There have been issues with the batters' strike rate. Pakistan used to rely on a particular winning method: the opening pair of Mohammad Rizwan and Babar Azam would set a platform, albeit often at a lower strike rate, but the team would post middling totals, and then the bowling would usually bail them out of trouble. However, the bowling arsenal is not as potent and consistent as it used to be. The bowling lacked the kind of discipline that we saw in the 2022 World Cup. The percentage of full tosses, half-volleys, and missed wide yorkers was higher in the last game, which invariably released all the pressure. Shadab Khan, in his current form as a bowler, is not providing the stability that Pakistan expects from an experienced bowling all-rounder. Abrar Ahmed could be a much better wicket-taking option, and he is capable of bowling in the powerplay. What do you think?
